Why this change

Bank-driven + CBPR+ Nov 2026 mandate. Banks will reject XML payment files with only unstructured <AdrLine> addresses starting November 2026 (ISO 20022 CBPR+).

UNESCO runs 3 custom DMEE trees in P01 that emit Hybrid or Unstructured addresses today. The migration must ensure at least <TwnNm> + <Ctry> (mandatory) and preferably full 5-tag structured PstlAdr.

The 3 XML payment file formats — what each one is for

UNESCO uses three distinct DMEE-generated XML payment formats in P01, each tied to a specific bank relationship and payment use-case. They are not interchangeable: T042Z routes each (company code, payment method) tuple to exactly one tree, and each tree produces a file format the receiving bank is expecting. Volumes below are from process mining of REGUH 2025+2026Q1 production payments.

Dbtr ✓ and Cdtr ✓ already structured in V000 — no changes there. ZERO ABAP for the CdtrAgt fix.

Why three formats and not one? Each receiving bank specifies its own pain.001 dialect (SEPA scheme is strict EUR-only; Citi adds proprietary tags for Worldlink cover-payment routing; CGI is the multi-bank common denominator). T042Z (263 rows in P01) is the routing brain — given (company code + payment method + LAND1), it picks the tree. SAP supports multiple PMW tree definitions per system precisely because real-world bank diversity demands it. UNESCO's three trees reflect three distinct bank rails — SocGen-EUR, Citi-USD/Worldlink, and the CGI multi-bank rail — not a duplication.

All three need adjustment for CBPR+ Nov 2026. The nature of the V001 change is asymmetric per format:

  • SEPA — biggest add: full Dbtr restructure (Hybrid → Structured) + Event 05 wiring. ~4 hours config.
  • CITI — medium add: Dbtr restructure (Unstructured → Structured) + UltmtCdtr StrtNm fill. XSLT post-proc handles empties automatically. ~4 hours config total.
  • CGI — smallest add: only CdtrAgt PstlAdr needs structuring. Dbtr + Cdtr already done in V000 (CGI is the existing pattern we lift to SEPA + CITI). ~3 hours config.
  • Plus 3 ABAP lines in YCL_IDFI_CGI_DMEE_FALLBACK_CM001::GET_CREDIT (Pattern A guard) — one transport, applies to all three trees.

Compliance states (3 states, not 2) — for context only

StateValidity after Nov 2026UNESCO position
Unstructured (AdrLine only)REJECTEDCurrent V000 state, migrate away
Hybrid (TwnNm+Ctry + AdrLine mixed)OK — minimum viableRejected as default — mixes legacy+new in one file; rollback + bank validation harder. Kept as fallback if V001 fails bank acceptance on specific vendors.
Fully structured (5 tags)OK + future-proofOUR TARGET (V001) — clean file, future-proof, DMEE-native versioning enables parallel V000/V001 operation + atomic cutover

Coexistence strategy — 2-file + DMEE native versioning (user-directed)

Instead of mixing structured+AdrLine in one file (Hybrid), V000 (current) and V001 (new) cohabit as two DMEE versions of the same tree, controlled by the DMEE_TREE_NODE.VERSION column and a single EX_STATUS flip at cutover. The full mental model — what V000/V001 mean, how the flip works, why D01 already has dormant V001 rows, visual proof — lives in DMEE Configuration · the version thing (single canonical source).

The strategy-level commitment here: V000 stays ACTIVE during Phase 2-4 (production untouched); test F110 runs reach V001 via a Z-payment method; at Phase 5 cutover the EX_STATUS flips atomically; rollback is the same flip in reverse; V000 decommissions 30 days after stable cutover. Stateful BAdI logic must be structure-aware (see ↳ Tree 3 · CGI for Pattern A fix on YCL_IDFI_CGI_DMEE_FALLBACK_CM001 name-overflow guard).

DME · Concepts & Runtime Flow

Start here — what problem does DMEE actually solve?

Every time UNESCO pays a vendor electronically, a file has to leave SAP and reach the bank. The bank dictates the exact shape of that file — what fields, what order, what separators, what character set, whether it's flat-text or XML. Société Générale wants pain.001.001.03 XML. Citi wants their CITIPMW V3 XML envelope. A Botswana bank wants a comma-separated flat file. The same payment data has to be re-shaped differently for each receiving bank.

Before DMEE, every new bank format meant ABAP development: a developer wrote a function module that hand-coded the file structure. Adding a new country or upgrading a format was a change request, a transport, code review, regression testing. Slow and expensive.

DMEE flipped this on its head. Instead of code, the file format is described as a tree — a drag-and-drop visual model where each node says "this part of the file gets this field from the payment data". A functional consultant can build or modify a tree without writing ABAP. The engine reads the tree at runtime and produces the file.

Two engines, one team — DMEE vs PMW

People often blur DMEE and PMW together, but they do different jobs.

  • DMEE (Data Medium Exchange Engine, Tx DMEE; called DMEEX in S/4HANA) is the format describer. It owns the tree — the shape of the bank file. It does not know when to fire or which payments go through it; it just knows "given a payment, produce a file in this shape".
  • PMW (Payment Medium Workbench) is the orchestrator around DMEE. It tells F110: "for this country + payment method + company code combination, use that DMEE tree, with this selection variant, and write the output to that file path." PMW also handles non-DMEE formats (legacy code-based — DTAUS0, ACH classic — used before DMEE existed).

Think of it like Word + Mail Merge. DMEE is the document template. PMW is the Mail Merge config that says "when sending letters to French vendors in October, use this template, with this address book, save to that folder." You can change the template without touching Mail Merge, and you can re-route Mail Merge to a different template without touching the template.

The bridge between the two is a single flag in OBPM1 called "Mapping using DME engine". When that flag is on for a PMW format, PMW knows to look up a DMEE tree with the same name. When it's off, PMW falls back to an old ABAP function module. UNESCO's four production trees are all DME-engine flag = ON.

Where the tree actually lives — four tables you should know

A DMEE tree is data, not code. It lives in four customizing tables:

  • DMEE_TREE_HEAD — one row per (tree, version). Defines tree-wide settings: name, source structure, charset, root-node ID, optional XSLT post-processor.
  • DMEE_TREE_NODE — one row per node. The bulk of the tree. Each row says "I am element X, my parent is Y, I read field Z from structure W, here's my length and conversion rule."
  • DMEE_TREE_COND — one row per condition. Rules like "suppress this node if the source field is blank" or "use this branch if country = FR".
  • DMEE_TREE_SORT — sort/key fields per level (e.g. group payments by company code at level 1).

For UNESCO, P01 holds: 1,975 nodes across 4 trees, 614 conditions, 39 sort entries. That whole landscape is what V001 surgically modifies.

End-to-end runtime — what happens when you press F8 in F110

F110 (SAPF110S → SAPFPAYM)
  ├ reads FBZP customizing (cocode + payment method)
  ├ selects open items, builds REGUH/REGUP, posts payment docs
  └ calls Payment Medium driver SAPFPAYM with OBPM4 selection variant
       ↓
SAPFPAYM
  ├ reads OBPM1 → format name + "Mapping using DME engine" flag
  ├ reads OBPM2 → note-to-payee rules
  ├ reads OBPM3 → customer FM enhancements
  ├ if DMEE flag = X → load tree where TREE_ID === OBPM1 format name (invariant)
  └ builds FPAYH / FPAYHX / FPAYP / FPAYP_REM / FPAYPX / DMEE_PAYD per (paying-cocode, vendor, item)
       ↓
DMEE controller (CL_DMEE_CONVERSION etc.)
  ├ traverses DMEE_TREE_NODE rows for active VERSION
  ├ resolves source: MP_SC_TAB + MP_SC_FLD + MP_OFFSET
  ├ applies CV_RULE conversion (CL=lowercase, AL.2=amount-align, RP=replace)
  ├ fires DMEE_TREE_COND (suppress / branch)
  ├ calls MP_EXIT_FUNC (BAdI / FM) when registered
  ├ assembles flat record OR XML element tree
  └ if XSLT registered (SF_NAME / XSLTDESC) → post-process (typical: prune empty leaves)
       ↓
FILE OUTPUT — TemSe / file system / FDTA download
  UNESCO: \\hq-sapitf\SWIFT$\P01\input\<cc>_<pm>_<fmt><date><seq>.in
  Botswana sandbox: C:\INT\Outbound\EFT\MVAEFT_161123_154701
       ↓
BCM batch → workflow 90000003 → Alliance Lite → SWIFT

Read this in plain English: F110 picks the open invoices, decides who to pay, posts the accounting documents, and then hands off to a separate driver report (SAPFPAYM) whose only job is to produce the bank file. SAPFPAYM looks up the configuration in OBPM1-4, fills in-memory structures with the payment details, and asks the DMEE engine to walk the format tree. The engine reads node by node — like reading a recipe — and either writes a literal value, reads a field from the structures, or calls a custom function for special cases. The result is a flat or XML file written to the file system, ready to be sent to the bank.

Why we're walking through all of this — anchoring V001 to the real machinery

V001 is not a redesign. It is a surgical change to specific points on the chain above. Knowing which point each change touches is what lets us bound the risk:

  • The Pattern A BAdI fix (3 lines in YCL_IDFI_CGI_DMEE_FALLBACK_CM001::GET_CREDIT) lives at the "calls MP_EXIT_FUNC" step. Affects only nodes whose MP_EXIT_FUNC = FI_CGI_DMEE_EXIT_W_BADI + the FALLBACK country dispatch path. Blast radius: bounded.
  • The SEPA Sub-option A (one TFPM042FB row) lives at the "OBPM3 / event-module wiring" step. Adds the SEPA tree to the existing Event 05 wrapper that already serves CGI. Blast radius: SEPA tree only.
  • The structured Dbtr nodes (5 per tree in V001) live at the "resolves source via MP_SC_TAB+MP_SC_FLD+MP_OFFSET" step. They read the same FPAYHX-REF01/REF06 buffer that already serves Cdtr. Blast radius: V001 nodes only — V000 untouched.
  • The empty-suppress conditions (5 per tree for SEPA) live at the "fires DMEE_TREE_COND" step. CITI skips them because CGI_XML_CT_XSLT auto-prunes empty leaves; SEPA has no XSLT, so it has to suppress at the tree level. Blast radius: SEPA tree only.

None of this is new SAP machinery. We are not inventing capabilities — we are using the SAP-standard hooks the way SAP designed them to be used. That is precisely why the risk profile is LOW.

Full source: knowledge/domains/Payment/dme_creation_payment.md §1 · adds canonical SAP-side scaffolding to existing UNESCO claims 96/99/102.

PMW Transactions — the 4 doors into the workbench

Why is PMW split across 4 separate transactions?

SAP could have put everything in one giant config screen, but they didn't — and that turned out to be a good thing. Each of OBPM1, OBPM2, OBPM3, OBPM4 owns a clean, separable concern. Once you know which transaction owns what, debugging becomes pinpointable: "the file format itself is wrong" → OBPM1 + the DMEE tree; "the note-to-payee text is missing" → OBPM2; "I need a custom field that isn't in FPAY*" → OBPM3; "the file went to the wrong folder" → OBPM4.

▸ OBPM1 — the format catalog

Think of OBPM1 as the library catalog for all bank-file formats SAP knows about. Each row is a "format" — a name like CGI_XML_CT or CHECK_BW — with three key attributes: which country it serves, whether it is DMEE-based or legacy code-based, and what event modules to call. The most important field is the "Mapping using DME engine" flag. When checked, SAP knows: "for this format, look up a DMEE tree with the same name and use it." When unchecked, SAP uses an old function module instead.

The invariant nobody tells you explicitly: when DME flag = ON, the OBPM1 format name must equal the DMEE TREE_ID character-for-character. /SEPA_CT_UNES in OBPM1 must match /SEPA_CT_UNES in DMEE_TREE_HEAD. If they drift apart (typo, rename) the format silently stops producing files. This is exactly why we proposed adding the brain feedback rule feedback_dmee_pmw_treeid_invariant as part of this work.

UNESCO touch-point: OBPM1 has rows for /SEPA_CT_UNES, /CITI/XML/UNESCO/DC_V3_01, /CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO, /CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO_1 — all DME-engine flag = ON. V001 does NOT touch OBPM1 — only the underlying tree.

▸ OBPM2 — note to payee rules

The note to payee is the human-readable line on a payment that tells the receiving party what the money is for ("Invoice #4711, October consulting"). Different payment formats need different note compositions: SEPA wants up to 140 chars in <RmtInf><Ustrd>, MT101 wants something else, a flat file might want a column-fixed extract. OBPM2 is where you say "for this format, build the note-to-payee by concatenating these fields with this separator, with this max length."

The OBPM2 output ends up in the in-memory structure FPAYP_REM — and that is the field DMEE reads when a node is mapped to <RmtInf><Ustrd>. So if you ever wonder "why is my Ustrd content wrong?", the answer is almost always at OBPM2, not in the DMEE tree.

UNESCO touch-point: OBPM2 drives the Ustrd content for our PPC countries (ID / IN / JO / MA / MY / PH). NMENARD's PPC dispatcher writes positional building blocks (SEPARATOR, FIXED_VAL, PPC_VAR, PPC_DESCR, PAY_FIELD) that ultimately surface here. V001 must preserve all OBPM2 wiring; we do not change it.

▸ OBPM3 — customer enhancements (the BAdI alternative)

OBPM3 lets you register a customer function module for a given format. The FM gets called at specific events during file creation — typically Event 05 (one shot per payment, where you can populate buffers like FPAYHX_FREF). Why does this exist when DMEE already has MP_EXIT_FUNC on individual nodes? Because they cover different scopes:

  • OBPM3 customer FMs = "do something once per payment / per file" (populate buffers, validate, side-effect logging).
  • DMEE node MP_EXIT_FUNC = "do something for this single field/value" (per-node transformation, conditional override, lookup).

They are independent extension points. When tracing a custom value, future agents must check both. UNESCO uses both: SAP-std OBPM3 FMs (e.g. FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_CGI_05 for Event 05) and per-node exits (e.g. /CITIPMW/V3_CGI_CRED_STREET on CITI tree nodes).

▸ The 7 DMEE lifecycle events — what each one is actually for

OBPM1's "Event Modules for Payment Medium Formats" sub-folder is where the 7 SAP-standard lifecycle events are wired to function modules per format. Think of file creation as a play: the curtain rises (Event 20), each scene plays out (Event 30 per record), the stage gets reset between acts (Event 25), and the curtain falls (Event 40). Two more events fire before the curtain even rises: validation (Event 10) and per-payment data prep (Events 00 + 05). For each event, you can register one custom function module that will be called when the event fires.

Each event has a single, well-defined purpose. You do not register all 7 — you register only the ones you have custom logic for. The screenshot below shows the SAP-std catalog (left popup) and the 6 events that /CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO has registered (right pane). UNESCO skips Event 10 entirely because there is no custom format-parameter validation needed for our flows.

EventPlain-English purposeWhen it firesUNESCO `/CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO`
00 · Fill sort field Populate the sort/key fields used to group payments at each level of the output tree (e.g. group by paying-bank then by due date) Once per payment, before the tree starts traversing FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_00 ✅
05 · Fill additional reference fields ⭐ Populate the FPAYHX_FREF buffer (REF01..REF15) and FPAYP_FREF buffer that DMEE nodes will read from. This is where structured-address bytes are written into the in-memory buffer before the tree walks them. UNESCO V001 directly depends on this event. Once per payment, after Event 00 FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_CGI_05 ✅ ← V001 hook (Sub-option A reuses this for SEPA via TFPM042FB row)
10 · Check format parameters Validate run-level parameters before any file is written. If the FM raises an error, the entire run aborts before file creation Once, at run start (validation phase) Not registered — UNESCO has no custom validation here
20 · Start / file header Emit pre-tree header content when a file opens. For XML formats this is mostly a no-op (the XML declaration comes from the tree); used for flat-file envelopes Once per output file (file open) FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_20 ✅
25 · File close / open Cleanup/finalize at file boundary when one F110 run produces multiple files (e.g. one file per paying-cocode) At each file split during the run FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_25 ✅
30 · Order / transaction record Per-record custom processing during emission — fires once for every individual payment Per FPAYH row (one payment in the batch) FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_30 ✅
40 · End / file trailer Emit trailer information at file close — totals, control sums, EOF markers. For XML this typically just emits closing wrappers; for flat files this is the line-9 trailer record we saw earlier Once per output file (file close) FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_40 ✅

▸ The order events fire at runtime

Reading them in numerical order does not match the firing order. Here is the actual timeline of a single F110 → SAPFPAYM → file run:

① Event 10 — validate format params              (once, very early; aborts run if it fails)
② per-payment loop:
     Event 00 — fill sort fields                    (per payment)
     Event 05 — fill FPAYHX_FREF / FPAYP_FREF       (per payment)  ← UNESCO V001 hook
③ per-file loop (files split by cocode/method):
     Event 20 — write file header
     ④ per-record loop inside that file:
          Event 30 — per-transaction processing
          DMEE tree traversal — emit XML/flat record
     Event 25 — fires if another file opens (split boundary)
     Event 40 — write file trailer (close the file)

Read this in plain English: SAP first validates that the run can proceed (Event 10). For each payment in the batch it fills sort fields (Event 00) and address/reference buffers (Event 05). Then for each output file it opens with a header (Event 20), walks every transaction emitting records (Event 30 + DMEE tree), handles file boundaries (Event 25), and closes with a trailer (Event 40). The DMEE tree itself is invoked once per record inside Event 30 — the tree is the engine, the events are the orchestration around it.

▸ Where to find this in OBPM1

To inspect or edit which events a format has registered, open Tx OBPM1 → click into the format name → the left dialog tree shows "Event Modules for Payment Medium Formats". The right pane lists Event / Function module / Implementation. To add a new event, click New Entries and pick from the popup of 7 (the popup we see in the screenshot).

UNESCO V001 implication → V001 does not register any new event for the SEPA tree — it adds one row in TFPM042FB (OBPM4 territory) registering Event 05 = FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_CGI_05 for the SEPA tree, reusing the SAP-std FM that already serves CGI. That single row is what tells SAPFPAYM "when running SEPA, also call the country-dispatch chain that fills the structured-address buffer." Zero ABAP development is needed for this — the FM exists, the dispatch logic exists, we are just pointing the SEPA tree at the same wiring.

▸ OBPM4 — selection variants for the driver report

This one trips people up because the name "Selection Variants" sounds optional. It is not. Every PMW format must have at least one OBPM4 entry per paying-cocode, otherwise F110 will run successfully, post the documents, and then quietly fail to write any bank file. The variant is what tells the SAPFPAYM driver: "for this run, use format X, write the file to path Y, with file name pattern Z, and please include a payment summary printout."

The variant ID is just a label (e.g., TESTING in the screenshots below). What matters is the variant's content: format name, file-name pattern (e.g. <cc>_<pm>_<fmt><date><seq>.in), and the "Output to file system" flag. Change the file path here, F110 writes to a new path next run.

UNESCO touch-point: F. Spezzano owns the parallel work on TFPM042F* (the table behind OBPM4). For V001, SEPA Sub-option A requires one new row in TFPM042FB registering Event 05 for the SEPA tree. That single addition is what lets the same SAP-std Event 05 wrapper that already serves CGI also feed FPAYHX_FREF for SEPA — meaning we do not need to write any custom Event 05 code for SEPA.

Quick-reference table

TxOwnsUNESCO V001 impact
OBPM1Format catalog · DME-engine flag · event modules. Format name === DMEE TREE_IDNone — V001 keeps existing format rows
OBPM2Note-to-payee composition rules · feeds FPAYP_REMNone — V001 preserves all PPC wiring
OBPM3Customer FM enhancements · per-event hooksNone directly (Event 05 already wired for CGI)
OBPM4Selection variants · file path · output flags+1 row in TFPM042FB registering Event 05 for SEPA tree (Sub-option A)

What each screen actually looks like

The four screenshots below are from a Botswana sandbox (cocode MVAF, format CHECK_BW), not UNESCO P01 — but the SAP UI is identical. We use them because they're publicly available and let us tag concepts visually. UNESCO's own screens look the same; only the format names and cocodes differ.

Walk through them in order: SPRO IMG path (where you start), OBPM4 catalog (where you pick the format and add a variant), variant creation popup (the moment SAP commits the new variant), SAPFPAYM variant editor (where the file path and output flags actually get set).

Right pane: format CHECK_BW (DME format tree for Botswana), variant table with pCo=MVAF, Sel.variant=TESTING. FBZP chain — three locks in series

The mental model — why three layers and not one?

Imagine SAP needs to answer one apparently simple question: "Should F110 pay vendor 12345 in company code UNES using payment method S?" Three separate parties might disagree:

  • The country regulators — France allows SEPA, but maybe not domestic checks; Saudi Arabia mandates IBAN, etc.
  • The company itself — UNES might say "I support SEPA, but only for amounts up to €1M and only via this house bank."
  • The vendor — Vendor 12345 might only accept wire transfer; cheques will bounce back.

SAP models all three as three independent locks. F110 walks down the chain at runtime: "Is method S allowed in country FR? Yes. Is method S allowed in cocode UNES? Yes. Does vendor 12345 list S as an allowed method? Yes. → Pay." If any one of the three says no, the payment is skipped. All three must agree.

Most "why isn't this vendor being paid?" tickets resolve to one of the three locks being misconfigured. Knowing which lock to check first saves hours.

The three locks at a glance

  1. Country-level payment method (Tx FBZP / OBVCU) — single-letter codes that say "in this country, payment method X means this kind of payment, uses this output (PMW vs classic), allows these currencies and document types." UNESCO's S/N/J/L/X codes live here.
  2. Cocode-level payment method (Tx FBZP / OBVU) — each cocode declares "yes, I support method X — and here are my amount limits, my grouping rules, my foreign-payment rules, and crucially my FBZP form binding (the field that says 'use DMEE, not legacy code')."
  3. Vendor-level binding (Tx FK02 / XK02) — the vendor master row carries the list of payment methods the vendor accepts plus optional house-bank override.

Lock #1 — Country-level catalog

This is where SAP keeps the "rule book per country" for payment methods. A single-letter code (or symbol — SAP uses things like &, =, @ as well as letters) is bound to a payment-method type (check / wire / SEPA / IHC), an output channel (PMW with a specific format, or legacy code-based), allowed currencies, and the document type to use when posting.

You read it as: "In country DE, code 5 means SEPA Credit Transfer using PMW format X." The code is short because it lives in single-character columns (REGUH-RZAWE, LFB1-ZWELS, etc.) that are hard to expand without massive regression.

erp_135.png — Country payment methods popup. Selection dialog opening with Paying co. code = MVAF, Pymt Method = C being entered. Behind it, the catalog shows the country's full set of methods: & SEPA Credit transfer · 5 SEPA Credit Transfer · 7 SEPA Credit Transfer (PE) · = MT101 · @ ISO 20022 International · C International Check · I/J Banküberweisung intern/extern IHC · L Auslandsüberweisung · M Auslandsüberweisung PMW. Tag: this is the country-level catalog. The cocode level (next screen) picks from this list.

Lock #2 — Cocode-level binding

Here each company code declares which payment methods (from the country catalog) it supports, and configures the operational details: amount limits, item-grouping rules, foreign-payment permissions, bank-selection optimization, and — most importantly for our DMEE work — the FBZP "form" fields.

erp_136.png — Maintenance of Company Code Data for a Payment Method (the list view). Rows: (Cocode, City, Pmt method, Name) — e.g. MVAF Gaborone C check, NAS2 New York 0 Biller Direct, NDF0 Harare C Cash Payment, NICK Frankfurt & SEPA Credit transfer. New Entries button highlighted at top-left. Read this as: "MVAF supports method C (check), NAS2 supports method 0, NICK supports SEPA …". UNESCO has rows here for every (UNES / IIEP / UIL) × every payment method (S / N / J / L / X) combination.
erp_137.png — FBZP detail for (MVAF, C check). Click into a row from the list and you get this screen. Amount limits (Min 300, Max 3 000 000 BWP) — F110 won't process invoices outside that range. Grouping of items (Single payment for marked item / Payment per due day / Extended Individual Payment) — controls whether one payment file lumps multiple invoices together or keeps them separate. Foreign payments (Foreign business partner / Foreign currency / Vendor bank abroad) — required for cross-border. Bank selection control (No optimization / Optimize by bank group / Optimize by postal code) — controls how F110 picks among the cocode's house banks. The Form Data button (highlighted) opens the section in the next screenshot — that is the section that says "use DMEE."

Pause here for a key insight → Everything you have seen so far on this screen happens before DMEE is even called. F110 uses these settings to decide which invoices to pick, which house bank to use, whether to group, and so on. Only after F110 has resolved all of that, and posted the documents, does it hand off to SAPFPAYM, which then asks DMEE to produce the file. So if your DMEE output is missing payments, the bug is upstream of DMEE — usually here in FBZP.

erp_138.png — same screen, Form Data section expanded. Two fields under Forms: Form for the Payment Medium (here blank) and Next form = SAPscript FPAYM_INT_DMEE. This is the DMEE switch. When FPAYM_INT_DMEE appears in either field, F110 routes this (cocode, payment method) combination through SAPFPAYM → DMEE. When the field is blank or set to a non-DMEE form name, F110 falls back to the legacy code-based PMW driver and never even loads a DMEE tree. If a future agent asks "why isn't DMEE firing for this payment?" — this is the first field to check.

Lock #3 — Vendor-level binding

Even if the country and cocode both allow a payment method, the vendor still has the final say. Vendor 200135 might only accept wire transfers (method T) and reject checks. The vendor master row carries an explicit list of allowed payment methods plus an optional override of which house bank to pay through.

erp_144.png — FK02 Change Vendor: Payment transactions Accounting for vendor 200135, cocode MVAF. Automatic payment transactions section: Payment methods = C (highlighted with arrow), House Bank = FB00. Tag: third lock. UNESCO vendor masters in P01 carry the S/N/J/L/X allowed lists; per-vendor LFB1.HBKID overrides force a specific house bank when the vendor demands it (e.g. UNESCO's intercompany vendors that must pay via FB00 only).

Putting it together — what F110 actually does

When F110 runs and hits vendor 200135 with an open invoice in cocode MVAF and proposed method C, it walks all three locks in order:

① country-level — "Is C allowed for cocode MVAF's country?"  → look up FBZP country table.
② cocode-level — "Does MVAF support method C? With what limits?
                   And does the form field say DMEE or legacy?"  → look up FBZP cocode table.
③ vendor-level  — "Does vendor 200135 list C as allowed?"        → look up LFB1 / LFA1.

If any → no, skip the invoice.
If all → yes, post payment doc, hand off to SAPFPAYM with format from cocode.form_data.
                                                                          ↓
                                                               DMEE tree fires.

This is exactly the flow that produces the file we are modifying in V001. Knowing the path makes failure points easy to predict.

F110 → SAPFPAYM → DMEE → File — what actually happens at runtime

The 5-act play

A successful payment run is a tightly choreographed sequence. Each act has its own screen, its own logs, and its own failure modes. If you are debugging a missing file, knowing which act broke down narrows the search dramatically:

  1. Act 1 · Parameters — you tell F110 which invoices, for which cocodes/methods, on what date.
  2. Act 2 · Proposal — F110 simulates: which vendors get paid, which get blocked, with what amounts. No postings yet.
  3. Act 3 · Edit Proposal (optional) — you can manually block/unblock specific items.
  4. Act 4 · Payment Run — F110 actually posts the FI documents. REGUH and REGUP are populated.
  5. Act 5 · Create Payment Medium — SAPFPAYM is called, DMEE traverses the tree, file is written. This is where DMEE actually runs.

Critical to remember: Acts 1-4 succeed independently of DMEE. You can have a green payment run with no file produced. The "Create payment medium" checkbox on the Schedule popup is what wires Act 5 to fire automatically. If unchecked, you'll see green status everywhere and still have no bank file — a classic source of confusion.

Acts 1-4 — F110 itself

erp_145.png — F110 Automatic Payment Transactions: Parameters. Run Date 27.04.2017, Identification MVA3. Posting Date / "Docs entered up to". Payments control: Company codes=MVAF, Pmt meths=C, Next p/date=02.05.2017. Tag: a payment run is identified by (RUN_DATE, LAUFI) — at UNESCO the LAUFI suffix +++++R / +++++P / +++++O is what NMENARD's PPC dispatcher uses to pick PAY_TYPE (Replenishment / Payroll / Other) per YTFI_PPC_STRUC.
erp_146.png — F110 Schedule Proposal popup. Start date / Start time / Target computer / Create payment medium ✓. Tag: the Create payment medium checkbox is what triggers SAPFPAYM (and therefore DMEE) immediately after the payment run. If unchecked, payments are posted but no bank file emerges — must be (re-)triggered manually via F110 → Environment → Payment Medium, or directly with Tx SAPFPAYM.
erp_147.png — F110 Status tab after a successful run. All four lights green: Parameters entered / Payment proposal created / Payment proposal edited / Payment run carried out. "Posting orders: 1 generated, 1 completed". Tag: green here ≠ DME file produced; green = postings done. The DME file lives in TemSe/filesystem; verify in FDTA.

The four-green-lights trap → Many UNESCO support tickets come in saying "F110 ran fine but the bank says no file arrived." The screenshot above looks identical whether Act 5 succeeded or never fired. To confirm Act 5 actually produced a file, you must go to FDTA (next section) — never trust the F110 Status alone.

Act 5 — FDTA: where the bank file actually lives

FDTA stands for Fi Data medium Transfer Administration — clunky name, simple purpose: it shows you the inventory of bank files SAP has produced. You filter by run date, identification, format, etc. and see one row per generated file. From there you can: download to local disk, mark as "transferred to bank", view content, or re-export.

For UNESCO, FDTA is mostly used for ad-hoc downloads and post-mortem investigations. The day-to-day flow uses BCM Monitor instead, because BCM batches, signs, and ships files through workflow 90000003. But FDTA is always available as a fallback and is the canonical source of truth for "did SAPFPAYM actually write a file?"

erp_150.png — FDTA Data Medium Administration selection. Reference number / Paying company code / Bank country, Selections (Run Date, Identification, Format), checkboxes for Pymt.runs, Proposal runs, Data medium (not yet transferred / transmit to external / w/out acct stmt / with acct stmt). Tag: post-F110 file inventory. UNESCO ops can also use BCM Monitor for the BCM-batched flow, but FDTA still works for ad-hoc downloads.
erp_151.png — FDTA Data Medium Overview. Columns: Run On / Ident / Propos / Amount / Currency / Entered by / Receiver / Format / Date created / Seq. nu / Paying. Sample formats: SEPA_CT, CGI_XML_CT_PE, DTAUS0. Tag: Format column = PMW format ID = DMEE TREE_ID. UNESCO rows show /SEPA_CT_UNES, /CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO, /CITI/XML/UNESCO/DC_V3_01.
erp_153.png — FDTA Download to local disk dialog. Addnl info=0001-ACB, File name=C:\INT\Outbound\EFT\MVAEFT_161123_154701, Comment=Download already carried out. Tag: file-naming pattern is governed by the OBPM4 selection variant (see erp_142.png). UNESCO uses <cc>_<pm>_<fmt><date><seq>.in resolving to \\hq-sapitf\SWIFT$\P01\input\….
erp_154.png — actual DME flat file (Botswana ACB) opened in TextEdit: 
1,LOCAL,CR,23112016,154745
2,3070618,029,002,BWP,23112016,TJ01,DIRECTPAYT,2875.50,MVA FUND
3,57360028909,02828,23112016,BWP,2875.50,NOTWANE PHARMACY,MVA FUND
9,4,2875.50
Tag: a flat-file DME — line types 1 header, 2 paying instruction, 3 beneficiary, 9 trailer/footer. Each line = one DMEE segment; integers + CSV separator come from DMEE_TREE_HEAD.SEGM_DELIM etc. Contrast with UNESCO: UNESCO emits XML DMEs (pain.001.001.03 envelopes) — the line-types disappear and become nested <PmtInf>/<CdtTrfTxInf> blocks; the underlying mechanism (segments → records, atoms → values) is identical.

What V001 changes about Act 5

Almost nothing visible at this layer. V001 changes what ends up inside the file (structured Dbtr address tags appear instead of unstructured <AdrLine>), but FDTA still sees one file per payment, named the same way, in the same path. The only operational change post-cutover is that the file content has more nested XML elements. M_SPRONK and ops won't see different screens; the bank just stops rejecting our files.

Format Tree Anatomy — the Lego catalog

The mental model — Lego pieces and ways to fill them

If a DMEE format tree is a Lego model of a bank file, then this section is the catalog of pieces. There are 7 piece types (the shape) and 7 ways to fill each piece with a value (the content). Once you grasp these 14 concepts, every DMEE tree in the world becomes readable — you can open one cold and trace exactly where each output character comes from.

Beyond the pieces themselves, the engine also has two control mechanisms: conditions (rules to suppress or branch) and sorts (how to group/order the input data per output level). Plus the tree-wide header settings (charset, root node, optional XSLT) that govern the whole assembly.

Reading order suggestion: node types → mapping procedures → conditions/sorts → header → source structures. You'll see how V001 fits at each layer.

Node types (column DMEE_TREE_NODE.NODE_TYPE) — the 7 shapes

The first three (Segment group / Segment / Composite) are mostly relevant for flat files. The middle two (Element / XML attribute) are XML shapes. Atom and Technical node work in both worlds. UNESCO trees are all XML, so we mostly deal with Element / XML attribute / Atom / Technical node.

Node typeUsed forXML or flat?
Segment groupGroup of segments (e.g. one repeat per line item)Flat
SegmentOne record / line in target fileFlat
CompositeGroup of elements inside a segmentFlat
ElementA leaf field (flat) OR an XML tag (XML)Both
XML attributeSub-node of an element supplying tag attributesXML only
AtomMultiple values feeding one element OR conditional value selectionBoth
Technical nodeStores a value referenced elsewhere; never written to fileBoth

Mapping procedures (per node, columns MP_*) — the 7 ways to fill a piece

Each node carries a mapping procedure that tells the engine where the value comes from. Four of these are passive ("read this field, this constant, this aggregate"), three are active ("call code, build from atoms, contain other things"). UNESCO uses all seven across the four trees:

ProcedureWhat the node doesUNESCO example
No mappingPure container (grouping)<Document> wrapping the body
ConstantLiteral text in MP_CONSTxmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance"
Structure fieldRead MP_SC_TAB.MP_SC_FLD + MP_OFFSETMost Dbtr/Cdtr nodes — FPAYH-ZBUKR, FPAYHX-REF01[0..60], FPAYP-XREF3 (h18 PurposeCode)
Reference to tree nodeRe-emit value of node identified by MP_SC_NODE / MP_SC_REF_NAMEUltmtCdtr structured-name reuse
AggregationSum/count/min/max over levelTrailer <NbOfTxs>, <CtrlSum>
Exit moduleCall FM/method named in MP_EXIT_FUNCUNESCO: BAdI FI_CGI_DMEE_EXIT_W_BADI on 794/1,975 nodes (40%) → YCL_IDFI_CGI_DMEE_FR/DE/IT/FALLBACK/UTIL. CITI: /CITIPMW/V3_CGI_CRED_* family
Own mapping (atoms)Compose value from multiple atoms with conditionsNMENARD's PPC tag value built from YTFI_PPC_STRUC positional building blocks (SEPARATOR / FIXED_VAL / PPC_VAR / PPC_DESCR / PAY_FIELD)

Conditions & sorts — the engine's two control levers

The mapping procedures decide what a node outputs. Conditions and sorts decide whether a node fires and how the data is ordered.

  • DMEE_TREE_COND — per-node suppress / branch logic. Each row says "if argument 1 OPERATOR argument 2 then [suppress / continue]". A node can have multiple conditions linked with AND/OR. UNESCO V001 SEPA design relies heavily on this: 5 new conditions per tree to suppress empty structured elements ("if FPAYHX-REF01[60..80] = '' then suppress <BldgNb>"). The CITI tree avoids needing these because XSLT auto-prunes empty leaves; SEPA has no XSLT, so suppression has to happen at the tree level.
  • DMEE_TREE_SORT — per-level sort/key fields. Tells the engine how to group repeating data into output levels. UNESCO uses ZBUKR (level 1 — one batch per company code), AUSFD+HKTID (level 2 — group by due date and account), DOC1R (level 3 — order by payment doc reference). This is what makes the file emit one PmtInf block per cocode, with line items grouped sensibly underneath.

The header (DMEE_TREE_HEAD) — tree-wide settings + UNESCO's V000 values

The header is one row per (tree, version). It sets things that apply to the whole tree, regardless of which node fires: the source DDIC structure, root node ID, charset, XSLT post-processor, etc. Most fields are inherited from V000 to V001 by the SAP-std "Create Version" function, but that exact semantic is one of the open known-unknowns we registered (KU-2026-DMEE-B) — we want to verify field-by-field before cutover.

FieldRoleUNESCO P01 V000
TREE_TYPEPAYM for paymentsPAYM (all 4 trees)
TREE_IDFormat-tree name = PMW format name/SEPA_CT_UNES · /CITI/XML/UNESCO/DC_V3_01 · /CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO · /CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO_1
VERSIONCoexisting versions per treeP01: 000 only · D01: 000 + 001 (V001 already created as dormant byte-clone — claims 109+111). V001 has never been transport-released to V01/P01 (claim 102).
EX_STATUS'A' = activeA on all (V000 active)
PARAM_STRUCDDIC structure for source-field pickerFPM_SEPA (SEPA), FPM_CGI (CGI + CGI_1)
FIRSTNODE_IDRoot nodeN_4880705930 · N_3831274320 · N_5649723900 shared by CGI + CGI_1 → critical: any change to N_5649723900 affects both
SF_NAME / XSLTDESCXSLT post-processorEmpty for SEPA + CGI; CITI uses CGI_XML_CT_XSLT (12-line identity-copy with empty-leaf-prune)

Source structures available to TREE_TYPE='PAYM' — what the tree can read

When you build a tree of TREE_TYPE='PAYM' (the type used for payment formats), DMEE knows about a fixed set of in-memory structures populated by SAPFPAYM at runtime. These are the only fields the tree can map nodes to. Custom append fields (UNESCO's Z and Y prefixes) live inside these structures.

Memorize these six — every UNESCO node ultimately reads from one of them:

StructurePurposeUNESCO custom append fields
FPAYHPer-paying header (one per payment file batch)ZBUKR, HBKID, HWAER, ZBNKS (vendor bank country), ZSTRA (vendor street, exit-populated for UltmtCdtr)
FPAYHXExtended per-batch — buffers populated by Event 05FPAYHX_FREF: REF01..REF15 + CURNO. UNESCO byte layout — REF01[0..60]=street, [60..80]=building, [80..90]=postcode, [90..100]=region, [100..110]=house_num1; REF06[0..40]=city
FPAYPPer-line-itemXREF3 carries the ISO 20022 PurposeCode (h18 finding)
FPAYP_REMPer-line remittance / note-to-payee<RmtInf><Ustrd> source for NMENARD PPC countries
FPAYPXExtended per-line — FPAYP_FREF.REF01..REF05 (same Dbtr address per line)
DMEE_PAYDStandard note-to-payee structureOBPM2 binds this

Cross-link — putting SAP-standard back into UNESCO context

Why this section exists

The first five tabs explained DMEE/PMW from SAP's perspective — generic, applicable to any company on any version of SAP. This last tab does the opposite: it walks the same concepts back to our work. Every SAP-standard mechanism we just learned is anchored to a specific UNESCO claim, file, or design decision in this V001 project. Reading this tab confirms the bridge — that nothing in V001 is novel SAP development; it is all SAP-standard hooks used in a SAP-standard way.

The mapping at a glance

If you only read one table in this whole companion's DME submenu, read this one. Each row is a SAP-standard concept on the left, the UNESCO claim or document that uses it on the right. Click through to the file to see the evidence.

Brain — what got registered, and why these 4 questions matter

While building this companion section we identified 4 questions we cannot answer with certainty today. Rather than guess or skip them, we registered them as formal known-unknowns in the brain so any future agent — whether ours or a successor — can pick them up and close them. Brain went from 36 → 40 KUs; these 4 surface in brain_v2/brain_state.json Layer 6 on next session start.

Why each question matters in plain terms:

  • KU-DMEE-A · Auth profile for version create/activate — UNESCO has never released a DMEE version-bump transport (claim 102: 0/44 historical transports). D01 has dormant V001 entries from a past Create-Version event (claim 109), but Activate Version has never been exercised on UNESCO trees. The first time M_SPRONK opens Tree → Versions → Activate Version we don't actually know if her auth profile allows it. If it doesn't, Phase 2 stalls until BASIS adds the missing object. Fix early in the dry-run protocol or we lose a week.
  • KU-DMEE-B · Header field copy semantics — Create Version copies node rows but the SAP standard does not document whether all 26 header columns are copied verbatim. If a field like XMLEMPTYELEMENTPROCESSINGTYPE resets to default on V001 creation, V001 output behavior could silently diverge from V000 — possibly causing bank rejections post-cutover. Cheap to verify; expensive to discover late.
  • KU-DMEE-C · Customizing vs Workbench transport — Affects how M_SPRONK pre-allocates the 8 transports listed in the versioning procedure. Wrong type = re-create the transport, possibly under deadline pressure. One TADIR query closes it.
  • KU-DMEE-D · The actual SAP KBA body — Our synthesis covers ~95% of DMEE/PMW from public secondary sources. The 5% gap is the SAP-side authoritative wording. The user already offered to pull this from authenticated SAP for Me; once received we integrate the delta into knowledge/domains/Payment/dme_creation_payment.md §8.
KU IDQuestionPriorityResolution path
KU-2026-DMEE-AAuth profile for Tx DMEE menu Tree → Versions → Create / Activate / Deactivate VersionMEDIUMF_DMEE_NDP auth-object lookup + SU24 readout + D01 dry-run + SU53 trace
KU-2026-DMEE-BDo all 26 DMEE_TREE_HEAD columns copy verbatim from V000 → V001, or do any default-reset (HANDLE_BYTES, XMLEMPTYELEMENTPROCESSINGTYPE, …)?MEDIUMD01 sandbox dry-run with all-fields-populated test tree + diff DMEE_TREE_HEAD V000 vs V001
KU-2026-DMEE-CAre DMEE V001 changes Customizing (W) or Workbench (K) transports?LOWTADIR.KORRDEP for object-type DMEE + observe transport prompt during dry-run
KU-2026-DMEE-DWhat does the body of SAP KBA 3361880828 actually say beyond what secondary sources cover?LOWUser pulls authenticated KBA body from SAP for Me

Each KU carries full context, how_to_resolve, and related_objects in JSON, so any future agent reading brain_state.json can pick up the work without re-deriving the path.

Scope — what we change in V001

Why this section matters

The V001 project covers a deliberate, narrow change to UNESCO's payment-file generation: convert vendor / debtor postal addresses from a single unstructured <AdrLine> line to fully-structured ISO 20022 elements (<StrtNm>, <BldgNb>, <PstCd>, <TwnNm>, <Ctry>) before the CBPR+ Nov 2026 mandate kicks in. That is the entire goal. Everything in this tab is either a step toward that goal (IN SCOPE), a deliberate non-change to keep risk low (STAYS THE SAME), or an explicitly-deferred concern (OUT OF SCOPE).

The reason this scope is so tight is that UNESCO's payment infrastructure has been stable for years (claim 102: zero V001/V002 patterns across 44 historical transports). The bank deadline is real, but the cost of breaking working SocGen / Citi / SEPA flows would dwarf the benefit of getting V001 done quickly. Rule of thumb the team is following: if a change is not on the critical path to "structured address tags in the file", it does not go into V001 — even if it would otherwise be worth doing.

How to read the three sub-tables below

  • IN SCOPE — the actual deliverables. Each row is something a transport will carry, code review will approve, and Phase 3-4 will test. Effort estimates are realistic.
  • STAYS THE SAME — assets we explicitly chose not to touch. This is just as important as IN SCOPE because it's the surface we're protecting from regression.
  • OUT OF SCOPE — questions and changes the team agreed to defer. Each one has a documented rationale; some have brain claims that closed them.

✅ IN SCOPE — V001 changes (per tree)

Each row is one deliverable. The "Type" column tells you whether this is customizing (config tables / DMEE tree edits, no ABAP), code (ABAP development, code review needed), or data (master-data fixes, no transport). The vast majority is CONFIG — a deliberate design choice to minimize ABAP review burden.

TreeChangeTypeEffort
/SEPA_CT_UNES+5 Dbtr structured nodes (StrtNm/BldgNb/PstCd/TwnNm/Ctry) reading FPAYHX-REF01/REF06 with MP_OFFSET. +5 empty-suppress conditions in DMEE_TREE_COND (no XSLT for SEPA).CONFIG~4 hours

Total ABAP: 1 method, 3 lines. Total CONFIG: ~24 nodes (5 SEPA Dbtr + 5 CITI Dbtr + 1 CITI UltmtCdtr StrtNm + ~7 CGI CdtrAgt + 5 SEPA empty-suppress conditions) + 1 OBPM4 row + 5 vendor fixes.

Why these numbers matter → 1 method, 3 lines of ABAP. That is the entire code-change footprint. Everything else is config — which means M_SPRONK can deliver most of V001 without writing a single line of ABAP, and N_MENARD's review burden is bounded to a single 3-line guard. This was a deliberate design: the project's risk profile is minimised by pushing the work into config tables (DMEE_TREE_NODE / DMEE_TREE_COND / TFPM042FB) where SAP-std machinery does the heavy lifting.

⚖ STAYS THE SAME (V000 untouched)

This is the surface we explicitly do not touch. It looks like a long list, but each row is doing real work: the production payment flow keeps running on V000 the entire time V001 is being built and tested. SAP-standard FMs and country classes stay exactly as SAP shipped them. UNESCO's existing BAdI implementations (FR/DE/IT/UTIL) keep their behavior. The "STAYS THE SAME" list is the regression boundary: any UAT failure that traces back to one of these assets means V001 has overreached its scope.

AssetWhy preserved
All V000 DMEE treesProduction payment flow continues unchanged during transition. V000 only deactivates at Phase 5 cutover.
SAP-std FMs (FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_CGI_05, /CITIPMW/V3_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_05, GENERIC class, country classes FR/DE/IT/GB)SAP-delivered, never modified. Reused by V001.

❌ OUT OF SCOPE

Each item below was raised and consciously rejected for V001 — not forgotten. Some of these (Q3 UltmtCdtr, A1 per-bank strictness) were originally framed as "must answer before V001 design can close" and got resolved system-internally instead of via external SME ask. That follows the brain rule feedback_prefer_system_internal_to_external_sme : if a question is answerable from extracted data, answer it from data rather than waiting on bank or vendor SME response. Saved the project 2-4 weeks of bank-response wait time on each.

  • pain.001.001.09 schema migration — separate project (current trees stay on .03; simulator confirmed V001 forward-compatible with .09 — claim 105)
  • BCM workflow 90000003 modification — dual-control logic untouched
  • Bank file naming + transmission — Alliance Lite2 + SWIFT delivery untouched
  • ICTP Trieste trees (/SEPA_CT_ICTP_*) — separate from UNESCO HQ scope
  • Vendor master cleanup beyond the 5 mandatory-missing — V001 emit-empty + suppress-cond strategy handles 68.8% missing HOUSE_NUM1 cleanly without DQ pressure on V001 design
  • BCM_BATCH_* BAdIs — not extracted, not in change path
  • Per-bank acceptance gating — not a scope item under V001 Fully-Structured commitment. Fully-Structured (5 tags) strictly satisfies any CBPR+ bank strictness ≥ Hybrid (TwnNm+Ctry minimum) by ISO 20022 schema definition. Simulator 794/794 PASS on .03+.09. Brain claim 105. TRM emails reduced to 1-page logistics.

Removed from out-of-scope (Sessions #62-63): UltmtCdtr Worldlink (Q3) RESOLVED via DMEE_TREE_NODE system analysis (claim 99). Per-bank strictness (A1) CLOSED via V001 Fully-Structured commitment + simulator (claim 105). Both follow the pattern feedback_prefer_system_internal_to_external_sme HIGH — answer from system data, not from external SME ask.

Understanding the problem — Structured vs Hybrid vs Unstructured (CBPR+ ISO 20022)

Brain anchor: claim 113 · CBPR+ Nov 2026 mandate · ISO 20022 PstlAdr definitions. The three states below are the regulatory definitions banks enforce, not arbitrary labels. What banks actually look at: which structured leaves <StrtNm> <BldgNb> <PstCd> <TwnNm> <Ctry> exist as XML elements in the file. The <PstlAdr> container is mandatory; the children determine compliance.

CBPR+ stateDefinition (which leaves exist + populated)Bank acceptance post-Nov 2026Risk
UNSTRUCTURED Only <AdrLine> leaves emitted · NO <TwnNm> + <Ctry> structured leaves OR they are unpopulated REJECTED HARD STOP — bank rejects the file at SWIFT entry. No payment goes through.
HYBRID Both <TwnNm> AND <Ctry> structured leaves emitted with values (CBPR+ minimum mandatory) · remaining content (street, postal, building) inside <AdrLine> ACCEPTED (minimum viable) Some banks may flag for review · stricter banks (post-2027) may move to Reject. Not future-proof.
FULLY STRUCTURED All 5 ISO 20022 structured leaves emitted: <StrtNm> + <BldgNb> + <PstCd> + <TwnNm> + <Ctry> · <AdrLine> empty or suppressed ACCEPTED + future-proof Strict superset of Hybrid · forward-compatible with pain.001.001.09 schema · maximum bank acceptance margin.

Important nuance — the state is determined by tree configuration, not by data quality

A <PstlAdr> branch is Unstructured/Hybrid/Structured based on which structured-leaves EXIST as nodes in the DMEE tree (DMEE_TREE_NODE rows under the PstlAdr parent), not whether the data fields are populated for any given vendor. If the tree has no <StrtNm> leaf, the XML output never has one regardless of vendor data quality. This is system-data-driven, not observation-driven.

Implication for Marlies's analysis: her 10 production XML samples are sample-validation, not the classification authority. A tree may produce different-looking output for vendor A vs vendor B (because of vendor data variations), but the tree configuration is single-state. The CBPR+ classification of a tree is "what structured leaves can it possibly emit". This is what claim 113 enumerates per (tree, party).

Why V001 chose Fully Structured (not minimum-viable Hybrid)

  • Hybrid satisfies CBPR+ Nov 2026 minimum but is not bank-strictness-future-proof. Some receiving banks (especially in PPC countries — claim 99) may enforce stricter than CBPR+ minimum for AML reasons.
  • Fully Structured is a strict superset of Hybrid — accepted everywhere Hybrid is, plus accepted at strict gateways.
  • Per claim 105 commitment: V001 ships Fully Structured + empty-suppress conditions (so vendors with missing data still produce clean XML — empty leaves auto-removed via DMEE_TREE_COND for SEPA/CGI, XSLT for CITI).
  • Simulator (claim 105): 794/794 PASS on both pain.001.001.03 (current) and pain.001.001.09 (future) schemas — Fully Structured is forward-compatible.

Per-tree current state — system-data classification (not comment-based)

Derived from RFC-extracted leaf inventory in P01 V000 (claim 113, RFC verification 2026-04-30). For each tree × party, the structured leaves PRESENT in the tree determine the classification. If a structured leaf is missing in the tree, the XML output cannot have that element regardless of vendor data.

TreePartyStructured leaves PRESENTStructured leaves MISSINGCBPR+ classificationRejection risk post-Nov 2026

/SEPA_CT_UNESDbtrCtryStrtNm · BldgNb · PstCd · TwnNmUNSTRUCTUREDHARD STOP — REJECT
/CITI/.../DC_V3_01Dbtr-primaryPstCd · TwnNm · CtryStrtNm · BldgNbHYBRID+OK minimum · not future-proof
/CITI/.../DC_V3_01Dbtr-altMor (TECH)(none)StrtNm · BldgNb · PstCd · TwnNm · CtryUNSTRUCTURED (3× AdrLine only)HARD STOP when alt-mode fires
/CITI/.../DC_V3_01CdtrStrtNm · BldgNb · PstCd · TwnNm · Ctry · CtrySubDvsn(none)FULLY STRUCTUREDOK · BAdI/CITIPMW fills runtime

Total parties at HARD-STOP rejection risk under V000 today: 4 (SEPA Cdtr · SEPA Dbtr · CITI Dbtr-altMor · CGI CdtrAgt). Hybrid+ parties at future-proof risk: 3 (CITI Dbtr-primary · CITI UltmtCdtr · CITI CdtrAgt). V001 lifts all 4 hard-stop parties to Fully Structured + completes the 3 Hybrid+ to Fully Structured. Brain claim 113.

Change Strategy — HOW we deploy V001

Why we even need a strategy

If V001 were simply "edit the DMEE tree in production and turn it on", we wouldn't need this section. The reason we do is that UNESCO can never afford a payment day where bank files are rejected. Every payment cycle has hard deadlines (payroll, vendor invoices, intercompany sweeps); a single failed cycle costs money, reputation, and finance-team weekends. So the strategy has to answer three questions at once: (1) How do we put V001 in production safely? (2) How do we test it side-by-side with V000 before cutover? (3) How do we instantly roll back if a bank rejects V001?

The strategy below uses a SAP-native feature (DMEE tree versioning) that solves all three at once. It is not a custom workaround — it is the canonical way SAP intended bank-format upgrades to be deployed.

Why 2-file + DMEE versioning (not Hybrid single-file)

The team considered two main approaches before locking in. They look similar on paper but diverge sharply on rollback risk and bank validation. The decision was made user-directive on 2026-04-24:

ApproachAdopted?Why
Hybrid single file (mixed structured + AdrLine in same XML)❌ RejectedMixes legacy + new in one file → parser confusion, rollback hard, bank validation harder
2-file + DMEE native versioning (V000 + V001 parallel)✅ AdoptedPer user directive 2026-04-24. Atomic activation/rollback. SAP-native. Bank can validate V001 via test gateway without prod risk

Read this in plain English: the Hybrid single-file approach would have produced one file with both old and new tags mixed together — which sounds like belt-and-suspenders but actually makes the bank's parser job harder and our rollback nearly impossible (we'd have to re-emit the file). The 2-file + DMEE-versioning approach keeps V000 alive in parallel with V001 as two completely separate trees, lets us flip between them with one config change, and lets the bank validate V001 in a test gateway without ever touching the production V000 stream.

How V000 + V001 coexist — phase-by-phase timeline

The mechanism (V000 vs V001 cohabitation, EX_STATUS flip, dormant V001 in D01) is documented canonically in DMEE Configuration · the version thing. This section adds something specific to this strategy tab: the project-phase timeline — exactly which version is firing in each system at each project phase, so reviewers can trace operational risk over time:

Phase 2 (May 2026):
  Tree V000 = ACTIVE (current production state, unchanged)
  Tree V001 = INACTIVE (newly deployed dormant)

Phase 3-4 testing:
  Z-payment method routes test F110 → V001 only
  Production payments → V000 (untouched)
  Both files generated for parallel comparison

Phase 5 cutover (atomic):
  Deactivate V000, Activate V001 → instant
  All F110 now produces V001 structured

Rollback (instant if needed):
  Activate V000, Deactivate V001 → seconds, no data loss

Phase 5 + 30 days stable:
  V000 decommissioned

Read the timeline like this: during May 2026 we build V001 alongside the existing V000, with V001 deployed but turned off. During Phase 3-4 we route only test payments through V001 (using a Z-payment method that doesn't appear on real invoices) so we can compare V000 vs V001 byte-for-byte. At cutover (Phase 5) we flip the EX_STATUS flag — atomic, instant — and from that moment all F110 runs use V001. If a bank rejects, we flip back. Thirty days after stable cutover, V000 is decommissioned. The whole sequence is reversible until the V000 cleanup.

Per-tree strategy nuances

The four DMEE trees in V001 scope are not symmetric. Each one has its own quirks driven by either the bank's expectations (Citi uses an XSLT post-processor; SEPA does not), the tree's history (CGI shares a root node with its CGI_1 peer), or pre-existing custom logic (CITI tree has UltmtCdtr Worldlink node that was already half-wired). The table below makes the differences explicit so reviewers don't apply uniform thinking where the implementation has to differ:

TreeWhat V001 changesEmpty-element handlingWhy different
/CITI/XML/UNESCO/DC_V3_01 (Dbtr)+5 Dbtr structured nodesEmit all 5 nodes unconditionally. XSLT (CGI_XML_CT_XSLT) auto-removes empty.XSLTDESC populated for this tree only — verified Phase 1.
/CITI/XML/UNESCO/DC_V3_01 (UltmtCdtr Worldlink)+1 StrtNm = FPAYH-ZSTRA. Existing 7 nodes already populated (Nm, Ctry, TwnNm, PstCd, CtrySubDvsn, AdrLine1, AdrLine2). Q3 RESOLVED.Same XSLT auto-removal applies.System-driven Q3 resolution — UltmtCdtr was the last open question, now closed via DMEE_TREE_NODE inspection (N_8838338720, brain claim 99).
/SEPA_CT_UNES+5 Dbtr structured nodes + Sub-option A test (FI_PAYMEDIUM_DMEE_CGI_05 registration)Add explicit DMEE_TREE_COND per node: emit only if source field NE spaceNo XSLT for SEPA — empty nodes would be emitted as-is, breaking schema
/CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO + _1Fix CdtrAgt — PstlAdr from AdrLine to structured (StrtNm/PstCd/TwnNm/Ctry). Dbtr + Cdtr already structured ✓ — no Dbtr/Cdtr changes.CdtrAgt nodes use existing T012K/BNKA-driven Event 05 wiring. PRESERVE PPC tags untouched: <InstrForCdtrAgt><InstrInf> and <RmtInf><Ustrd> dispatch logic must not change.Plan §Per-tree design line 550. PPC system requires those tags to dispatch correctly for AE/BH/CN/ID/IN/JO/MA/MY/PH. ZERO ABAP for the CdtrAgt fix — all wiring is config-only.

⚠️ PPC preservation requirement — added 2026-04-29

Plain-English context: PPC stands for Payment Purpose Code — a regulatory tag that 9 specific countries (UAE, Bahrain, China, Indonesia, India, Jordan, Morocco, Malaysia, Philippines) require in the payment XML or the receiving bank rejects the payment. UNESCO has a working PPC dispatch system in production today (NMENARD specs Doc 2+3, March 2024) that writes country-specific values into <InstrForCdtrAgt><InstrInf> for AE/CN and into <RmtInf><Ustrd> for the other 7 countries.

The V001 CGI tree change touches <CdtrAgt><PstlAdr> (a different XML node — the creditor's bank address). But because both PPC and CdtrAgt sit inside the same <PmtInf><CdtTrfTxInf> wrapper, an over-broad refactor could accidentally break PPC routing. This callout is the explicit no-touch warning: V001 must NOT alter the BAdI dispatch behavior on:

  • <PmtInf><CdtTrfTxInf><InstrForCdtrAgt><InstrInf> (used by AE, CN PPC)
  • <PmtInf><CdtTrfTxInf><RmtInf><Ustrd> (used by BH/ID/IN/JO/MA/MY/PH PPC)

Without PPC, banks for the 9 countries above reject USD payments via SocGen. This is one of the strongest "do not touch" lines in the V001 design: a regression here means real payments to vendors in those countries fail until the next correction transport.

PPC verification approach — READ P01, no need to SIMULATE D01

User insight 2026-04-29: "podemos leer todo lo que ya pasó". The PPC system is DETERMINISTIC — we don't need F110 simulation in D01 to verify behavior:

  1. The algorithm is known: extracted source YCL_IDFI_CGI_DMEE_UTIL_CM003 (79 lines, byte-identical D01↔P01)
  2. The data is known: YTFI_PPC_STRUC (133 rules) + T015L (73 SCB indicators) extracted to Gold DB
  3. For any (LAND1, LZBKZ, PAY_TYPE) tuple: predict the expected PPC tag content by replaying the algorithm in Python
  4. Validate against P01 production: sample REGUH for PPC-country payments → read actual XML output via REGUC.VARDATA or DTA file history

D01 F110 simulation is only useful for verifying V001 STRUCTURAL changes (new PstlAdr nodes), NOT for re-confirming V000 PPC behavior. The PPC dispatch chain is already provably correct in P01 — we just need to ensure V001 tree changes don't alter the dispatch.

PPC validation — concrete script approach

# Pseudo-code for PPC validation script (Python on Gold DB):
for each REGUH row WHERE LIFNR has bank_country IN PPC_9_countries:
    # 1. Predict expected PPC tag content
    pay_type = derive_from_dorigin(fpayh.DORIGIN[0:2])  # HR→P, TR→R, otros→O
    deb_cre = 'C'  # always credit
    expected_value = ''
    FOR row IN YTFI_PPC_STRUC WHERE land1=bank_ctry AND pay_type=pay_type
                              AND tag_full=tag_xml_path
                              ORDER BY code_ord:
        if row.PPC_CODE = SEPARATOR/FIXED_VAL: append row.PPC_VALUE
        if row.PPC_CODE = PPC_VAR: append T015L[invoice.LZBKZ].ZWCK1.first_token
        if row.PPC_CODE = PPC_DESCR: append T015L[invoice.LZBKZ].ZWCK1.rest
        if row.PPC_CODE = PAY_FIELD: append fpay_struc[row.PAY_FIELD]
    # 2. Read actual XML output
    actual_xml = read_xml_file(reguh.LAUFD, reguh.LAUFI, reguh.ZBUKR)
    # 3. Compare
    assert actual_xml.tag(tag_xml_path).content == expected_value

This validation can be done NOW on P01 data (no Phase 2 prerequisite). It confirms V000 PPC works correctly. Then in Phase 3, V001 simulation in D01 needs only to verify that the same dispatch chain still fires — not to re-validate the algorithm.

Pattern A — the only ABAP change (BANK-MANDATED, confirmed 2026-04-29)

The "Pattern A" name comes from NMENARD's internal naming for an existing piece of UNESCO custom logic. Société Générale specifically demanded that when a vendor name exceeds 35 characters (the limit for <Cdtr><Nm>), the overflow goes into <StrtNm> (yes — into the street name tag, alongside the actual street). This is a SocGen quirk and not an ISO 20022 standard — but it is real, in production, and the bank has explicitly insisted.

The problem with V001: that overflow logic writes into <StrtNm>, but V001 also writes the structured street into <StrtNm>. Without the guard, V000's overflow would clobber V001's structured street. The 3-line guard fixes this: it tells the existing legacy code "only prepend the name overflow if StrtNm is empty (V000 case) — leave it alone if StrtNm is already populated (V001 case)". V000 production behavior is fully preserved; V001 gets correct structured StrtNm.

3-line guard in YCL_IDFI_CGI_DMEE_FALLBACK_CM001::GET_CREDIT. Prevents V001 structured StrtNm from being corrupted by V000's legacy name-overflow logic. Backward-compatible: V000 behavior preserved.

Origin confirmed (Q1 RESOLVED): per N_MENARD doc TS DMEE CGI modifications 20240229.docx, this overflow logic is a Société Générale-mandated requirement — the bank explicitly insisted on prepending Name1 chars 36-40 + Name2 to <StrtNm> when name >35 chars. A1 (remove) is NOT acceptable — would break SocGen production. A2 (guard) is the only valid path. Quote: "I don't think this is a very 'clean' solution but we asked confirmation by giving examples and they insist."

" Add this guard:
WHEN '<PmtInf><CdtTrfTxInf><Cdtr><PstlAdr><StrtNm>'.
  IF i_fpayh = mv_fpayh
     AND mv_cdtr_name+35 IS NOT INITIAL
     AND c_value IS INITIAL.            "← V001 GUARD: only prepend if StrtNm empty
    c_value = mv_cdtr_name+35.
  ELSEIF i_fpayh = mv_fpayh
     AND mv_cdtr_name+35 IS NOT INITIAL.
    c_value = |{ mv_cdtr_name+35 } { c_value }|.   " V000 legacy preserved
  ENDIF.
  IF c_value+70 IS NOT INITIAL.
    CLEAR c_value+70.
  ENDIF.

Reviewer: N_MENARD (code owner). Pending alignment call (see Phase 1 tab).

Test pyramid (4 levels of risk)

Testing strategy is layered like a pyramid: the bottom is cheap, fully-reversible synthetic testing in D01 read-only; each level above adds realism but also adds risk and external dependency. We move up the pyramid only after the lower level passes. The goal is to maximise the number of bugs caught at L0/L1 (where rolling back is free) and minimise reliance on L2/L3 (where transports or external banks are involved):

LevelWhereRiskExamples
L0 — DMEE Tx Test simulationD01 read-onlyZEROSynthetic FPAYHX payload, validate XML output. Python XSD harness.
L1 — D01 simulation no transportD01Reversible (no transport)F110 proposal mode with Z-payment method routed to V001
L2 — D01 transport, V01 test clientD01 → V01Transport-revertableReal F110 in V01 with Z-method, compare V000 vs V001 byte-by-byte
L3 — Bank pilot via test gatewayExternalExternal dependencySend V001 sample to bank's test gateway (separate from prod), get written acceptance

Cutover order (Phase 5)

The three trees do not cut over together. Sequencing matters: each tree's V001 activation has its own blast radius, and we deliberately go from narrowest impact to widest impact. If something goes wrong at step 1, only one tree is affected and we can roll back without disturbing the others. The 14-day buffer between cutovers lets us catch slow-burn bugs (delayed bank rejections, monthly reporting glitches) before extending the change to the next tree:

  1. CGI tree first — only 3-line BAdI fix activates effects. Lowest blast radius. Validate.
  2. SEPA second — first tree with full V001 node additions. UNESCO + IIEP + UIL.
  3. CITI last — highest volume + Worldlink edge cases. Most exposed if anything fails.

Each cutover: 14-day monitoring before next tree's cutover. Total Phase 5 window: ~6 weeks from first cutover (CGI) to V000 decommissioning after CITI stable.

Rollback protocol

The single biggest reason we chose 2-file + DMEE versioning over Hybrid is right here: rollback is a single config flag flip, atomic, and zero data loss. The protocol below tells the on-call team exactly what to look for, what to do, and who decides:

Detection criteria:
  - >2 bank rejects in 24h attributed to address structure
  - XSD validation failure rate >1%
  - Marlies/Treasury head override

Action sequence (≤60 minutes from decision):
  1. DMEE Tx → tree → V000 ACTIVE / V001 INACTIVE (atomic flag)
  2. Tx FDTA: re-run 1-vendor F110 sample, verify V000 file emitted
  3. Notify banks via BCM ops DL: "Reverted to V000 unstructured; new ETA TBD"
  4. INC ticket open; preserve V001 inactive for forensics

Decision authority: Marlies (BCM ops) + Pablo (technical) jointly.
Data loss: zero (F110 idempotent on REGUH).

Decisions baked into this strategy

Each bullet below is a question that was raised during V001 design and was closed by an explicit decision (with the closing rationale and brain-claim anchor). They're listed here as a reference for anyone joining the project mid-stream — read them as "these are no longer open questions; here's why":

  • Pattern A2 (guard, not remove) → Q1 RESOLVED. SocGen-mandated overflow logic must be preserved in V000. V001 guards prevents corruption.
  • FR/CM002 retrofit P01→D01 → Q1bis RESOLVED. Not a method swap — CM002 is the PPC dispatcher entry that was added to P01 in March 2024 but never came back to D01. Mandatory in D01-RETROFIT-01.
  • CGI CdtrAgt fix → V001 converts CGI <CdtrAgt><FinInstnId><PstlAdr> from AdrLine to structured. Dbtr + Cdtr already structured ✓ in V000 — no changes there. PPC tags preserved.
  • PPC tags preserved in V001 → CGI tree V001 must NOT alter dispatch on InstrForCdtrAgt/InstrInf or RmtInf/Ustrd nodes
  • Verification = read P01, not D01 simulation → algorithm + data deterministic, sample P01 to validate expected output
  • UltmtCdtr Worldlink (Q3) → RESOLVED (system-driven). DMEE_TREE_NODE analysis confirmed 7 active source fields under N_8838338720 (Nm=FPAYP-NAME1, Ctry=FPAYH-ZLAND, TwnNm=FPAYH-ZORT1, PstCd=FPAYH-ZPSTL, CtrySubDvsn=FPAYH-ZREGI, AdrLine1=FPAYH-ZSTRA, AdrLine2=FPAYH-ZORT2). 99.7% of BRL Worldlink payments fire UltmtCdtr/Nm. V001 fills StrtNm = FPAYH-ZSTRA (same as Cdtr/Dbtr). UNIFIED into V001 — NOT deferred to V002. No human/TRM input needed. Brain claim 99.
  • Per-bank strictness → confirmed Phase 1 (TRM responses)
  • Vendor master cleanup → 5 mandatory-missing only (LOW risk per DQ)
  • pain.001.001.09 schema upgrade → SEPARATE project, not in V001
  • 2-tree CGI variants (CGI + _1) → SYNC pattern, no independent design

DMEE Configuration — the version thing, in plain English

↪ Forward to DMEE Configuration · foundations for the three operations on V001, per-target simplified mapping, runtime buffers, PMW retrofit, step-by-step in tx DMEE, and the all-trees before/after table. This sub-tab covers only the version mental model — V000 vs V001, "Active version" vs "Maintenance version", what already exists in D01, and visual proof of claim 109.

The one-line takeaway: every change in V001 is a row added to or modified in DMEE_TREE_NODE — done in tx DMEE, captured as a workbench transport (R3TR DMEE, class K — confirmed via SAP help). No ABAP for the row-level work. The same XML segments (<Dbtr>, <CdtrAgt>, <Cdtr>, <UltmtCdtr>) stay where they are; we just put more children inside their <PstlAdr>.

⚠ SAP-OFFICIAL CORRECTION — the version mechanism is OVERWRITE, not a flag flip

Earlier sections of this companion described V001 activation as "an atomic flag flip on EX_STATUS that swaps Active ↔ Maintenance roles, with V000 preserved as dormant for instant rollback". That model is INCORRECT vs SAP-official ECC 6.0 DMEE behavior. Verified against SAP Help Portal (Version Management, Activating Format Trees), SAP Datasheet (function module DMEE_GET_BACK_ACTIVE_TREE_ABA), and SAP Community blogs. The corrected model:

Aspect Wrong model (earlier in this tab) SAP-correct model (per official docs)
Version label semantics "V000 and V001 are 2 cohabiting slots; labels are permanent; only EX_STATUS flag swaps which is active" V000 is ALWAYS the active version. V001 is ALWAYS the maintenance version. V002–V998 are archived historical snapshots. V999 is SAP-delivered. The labels are semantic roles, not slot numbers.
What activation does "Atomic flag flip on EX_STATUS — V000 → blank, V001 → 'A'. V000 row data unchanged." V001's content is saved as V000, REPLACING the previous V000. The old V000 is OVERWRITTEN. No flag flip — content replacement. (SAP Help: "When you activate the maintenance version (001), the system stores it as the active version (000), replacing the previous active version.")
V000 preservation "Automatic — V000 rows remain in DMEE_TREE_NODE after activation, dormant" NOT automatic. V000 is overwritten at activation. To preserve the old V000, you must run Generate Version on V000 BEFORE activating V001 → snapshot archived to V002 (or next free number).
Rollback mechanism "Atomic flag flip in seconds — same dialog, select V000 → flip back" Multi-step Version Management procedure: tx DMEE → Utilities → Versions → Version Management → select V002 snapshot → Retrieve (copies V002 content into V001) → Tree → Activate (V001 with snapshot content overwrites V000). Time: 5–15 min per tree depending on size. Requires P01 DMEE-change authorization.
Transport class "Customizing (W) for all DMEE_TREE_* changes" Workbench (K) — logical object R3TR DMEE, client-independent (despite being functionally customizing). Only TFPM042FB (matrix row 9) is true Customizing (W).

Sources (verified):

  • SAP Help Portal — Version Management (DMEE)
  • SAP Help — Activating Format Trees
  • SAP Help — Displaying and Using Versions (menu paths SE09 + Utilities Version Management)
  • DMEE_GET_BACK_ACTIVE_TREE_ABA function module (function group DMEE1_ABA)
  • Techlorean — DME Tree Configuration (Workbench transport, R3TR DMEE confirmation)
  • SAP Community — pain.001.001.09 update procedure

Implication for the V001 deployment strategy: a new mandatory pre-cutover step is required — Generate Version on the current P01 V000 BEFORE activating V001. Without this snapshot, V000 is unrecoverable after the cutover. The corrected implementation strategy is described in the next subsection (with visual evidence captures from UNESCO's actual SAP confirming the model). All earlier lifecycle/playbook content based on the "atomic flag flip" assumption has been removed from this tab; the corrected procedure replaces it. If you encounter remaining wording about "EX_STATUS flip" or "rollback in seconds" elsewhere in the companion (e.g., Strategy tab "Rollback protocol"), re-read through this corrected lens.

Visual evidence from UNESCO's actual SAP — tx DMEE screenshots verify the SAP-correct model

The corrected model above is not theoretical — it matches what tx DMEE in UNESCO's actual SAP shows step by step. Five screenshots taken from /CGI_XML_CT_UNESCO in UNESCO's ECC 6.0 system confirm: (a) the operator UI exposes only "Active / Maintenance" as roles, (b) the menu path is exactly Utilities → Versions → Version Management, (c) UNESCO's V001 is currently a byte-equal dormant clone of V000 created by FP_SPEZZANO on 2025-03-20 (claim 109 — visually confirmed via Compare).
